TAG:1-percentage
*1-Percentage*

*Q1.* If 35% of 60% of A is equal to 25% of 75% of B, then what is the ratio of A to B? (#revise)

(a) 25 : 28 ✔
(b) 7 : 12
(c) 12 : 7
(d) 28 : 25


Q2. If 45% of 50% of a number is 27, then what is the number?

(a) 160
(b) 180
(c) 150
(d) 120 ✔


Q3. By how much is 60% of 75 greater than 1/5 of 25?
  [Hint:
  37.5 + 7.5
  45
  Now, question says
  By how much is 45 is greater than 5
  45 - 4
  40 ]

(a) 37
(b) 38
(c) 40 ✔
(d) 34


*Q4.* If p% of (25 + q)% of 300 = 18% of 200 and q% of 180% of 40 = 36% of 50, then what is the value of (p – q)?
  [IMG:ad-per-q3.png ]
(a) 1
(b) -1 ✔
(c) 3
(d) -3


Q5. If 18 toys out of 75 toys are for boys and the rest are for girls, what is the percentage of girls toys?
  [Hint:
  57 is x% of 75
  x = (57 x 100) / 75
  x = 5700 / 75
  x = 1900 / 25
  x = 380 / 5
  x = 76 ]

(a) 18%
(b) 67%
(c) 57%
(d) 76% ✔


Q6. If a person’s salary increases from ₹200 per day to ₹234 per day, then the percentage increase in the person’s salary is:
(a) 15%
(b) 17% ✔
(c) 14%
(d) 16%


Q7. Shantanu’s income decreased from Rs 42,800 to Rs.37,236. Find the percentage decrease in his income.
  [Hint:
  #revise quick subtraction of
  42,800 - 37,236
  5564
  x% of 42,800 = 5564
  x = 556400 / 42800
  #revise quick cancellation of above ]

(a) 13% ✔
(b) 14%
(c) 11%
(d) 12%


*Q8.* Arun receives a monthly salary. The ratio of his expenditure to savings is 8 : 2. What percentage of his salary does he spend?
  [Hint:
  8x & 2x
  Let, 800 & 200
  Then, total = 1000 ]

(a) 40%
(b) 20%
(c) 60%
(d) 80% ✔


Q9. Lucas's monthly income is ₹42,500. If his income increases by 18% then find his new monthly income (in ₹).
  [Hint
  18% = 10% + 5% + 3%
  42,500 + 4,250 + 2125 + 1275
  #revise mental addition of above
  42,500 + 7,650
  50,150 ]

(a) 47,500
(b) 48,120
(c) 50,150 ✔
(d) 43,000


Q10. Ram received an annual salary of ₹ 48,580 in the year 2008. This was 25% more than his salary in 2007. What was his salary in 2007?
  [Hint
  125% of x = 48,580
  x = (48,580 x 100) / 125
  x = (48,580 x 4) / 5
  x = 9716 x 4
  x = 36,000 + 2800 + 64
  x = 38,864 ]

(a) ₹39,670
(b) ₹38,864 ✔
(c) ₹31,750
(d) ₹33,864


*Q11.* If 30% of Ravi's income is equal to 40% of Suresh's income, then 50% of Ravi's income is equal to what percentage of Suresh's income?
  [IMG:ad-per-q11.png #revise]

(a) 66 2/3 % ✔
(b) 33 2/3 %
(c) 66 1/3 %
(d) 33 1/3 %


Q12. If 70 is subtracted from 70% of a number, the remainder is 70. What is the number?
  [Hint:
  Let, number = 100x
  70x - 70 = 70
  70x = 140
  x = 2
  200 #revise ]

(a) 400
(b) 100
(c) 300
(d) 200 ✔


*Q13.* When 50% of first number is subtracted from 80% of second number, then the resultant becomes two-fifth of first number. First number is approximately ____ % of second number.
  [Hint:
  80y - 50x = 100x x 2/5
  80y = 90x
  y/x = 9/8

  8/9 x 100% #revise ]

(a) 88 8/9 % ✔
(b) 77 7/9 %
(c) 82 2/9 %
(d) 75 5/9 %


Q14. Two numbers are, respectively, 10% and 25% more than the third number. The ratio of the two numbers is:

(a) 22 : 25 ✔
(b) 19 : 25
(c) 23 : 25
(d) 18 : 25


Q15. Two numbers are respectively 61% and 35% less than a third number. The first number is what percentage of the second number?
  [Hint:
  39  65  100
  x% of 65 = 39
  x = (39 x 100) / 65
  60 ]

(a) 60% ✔
(b) 24%
(c) 48%
(d) 30%


Q16. Let x = 6/7 and let y = 1/x. y is ____ more than x.
  [Hint:
  y = 7/6
  IMG:AR-per-q16.png
  #revise ]

(a) 33.66%
(b) 33.33%
(c) 36.66%
(d) 36.11% ✔


Q17. A quantity 4/5 is changed to 5/6. How much percentage change is given to the quantity?
  [Hint: #revise
  Same ratio method like above,
  100/24
  4.166666 ]

(a) 4.73%
(b) 4.71%
(c) 4.17% ✔
(d) 4.37%


Q18. A man multiplied a number by 8/5 instead of 5/8. What is the percentage error in the calculation?
  [Hint:
  "instead of" ke badd wala original no hota hai
  IMG:AR-per-q18.png
  #revise ]

(a) 124%
(b) 162%
(c) 156% ✔
(d) 100%


Q19. A pupil multiplied a figure by 3/5 instead of 5/3. What is the percentage error in the calculation?
  [Hint: same as above
  25 : 9
  diff = 16
  (16 x 100) / 25
  64 ]

(a) 64% ✔
(b) 47%
(c) 58%
(d) 52%


Q20. If the numerator of a fraction is increased by 140% and the denominator of the fraction is decreased by 20%, the resultant fraction is 12/7. Find the original fraction.
  [Hint:
  IMG:AR-per-q20.png #revise ]

(a) 4/9
(b) 4/7 ✔
(c) 7/6
(d) 8/9


Q21. The salary of employees in a factory was reduced by 20% due to economic crisis. In order to have their salary back to original amount, it must be raised by:

(a) 25% ✔
(b) 20%
(c) 40%
(d) 12.5%


*AB Rule* - When one is increase by reduction other

Q22. By what percentage should a racer increase the speed to reduce the time by 25% to cover a fixed distance?
  [Hint:
  IMG:AR-per-q22.png #revise ]

(a) 33 1/3 % ✔
(b) 37 1/3 %
(c) 41%
(d) 31%


Q23. If the price of rice is raised by 20%, then by what percentage should a person reduce his consumption of rice so that his expenditure remains the same? (correct to one decimal place)
  [Hint:
  IMG:AR-per-q23.png #revise ]

(a) 14.7%
(b) 18.7%
(c) 16.7% ✔
(d) 12.7%


Q24. If A earns 33 1/3 % more than B, then B earns less than A by:

(a) 25% ✔
(b) 16 2/3 %
(c) 33 1/3 %
(d) 50%

---DPQ---

Q4. A number increased by 20% gives 240. Find the number.

(a) 200 ✔

(c) 240
(d) 250

(a) 92/119 ✔
(b) 23/28
(c) 28/23
(d) 119/92

TAG:2-percentage
*2-Percentage*

1. Ravi's salary was increased by 50%. After some time, his new salary was also increased by 50%. Find his gain percentage of salary.
  [Hint: #revise
  Ratio method
  IMG:AR-lec2-q1.png  

  Successive formula
  IMG:AR-lec2-q1-m2.png 

  *Special trick* (if both increase):
  +6%, +3%
  9.18% (add, mul.) #revise

  +7%, +4%
  11.28%

  +5%, +1%
  6.05 (not 6.50) #revise

  +20%, +10%
  30.200
  32.00 (transfer 2) #revise

  +30%, +20%
  50.600
  56% ]

(a) 125% ✔
(b) 100%
(c) 200%
(d) 150%


*2.* If each side of a cube is decreased by 12%, then the percentage decrease in its total surface area is:
  [Hint:
  if, Area(2D) -> 2 times
  Volume(3D) -> 3 times

  -12%, -12%

  Use formula
  -12 -12 + (12 x 12 / 100)
  -24 + 1.44
  -22.56 (minus 2, then 56)

  Tip: -12 -12 = -24
  add anything to -24, it will less than it,
  then go by option
  #revise ]

(a) 25.66%
(b) 28.23%
(c) 22.56% ✔
(d) 26.54%


3. A number is increased by 25% and then decreased by 16%. By what percentage is the resulting number less than/more than the original number?
  [Hint:
  formula: a + b + (a x b / 100)

  25 - 16 - (15 x 16 / 100)
  9 (+ve)
  Now, some digit minus from 9
  so, answer will be in positive and < 9
  go by options
  #revise ]

(a) does not change
(b) decreases by 5%
(c) increases by 5% ✔
(d) decreases by 13%


*4.* The breadth of a rectangular lawn is decreased by 8% and its length is increased by 15%. Find the percentage change in the lawn area.
  [Hint: as above
  15 - 8
  7 (+ve)
  less than 7 and +ve
  go with options #revise ]

(a) 8.5% increase
(b) 8.5% decrease
(c) 5.8% decrease
(d) 5.8% increase ✔


5. If the radius of a sphere is increased by 12%, then the volume will be increased by approximately:
  [Hint:
  Volume -> 3D
  3 times successive

  *trick for 3 times same successive*
  3a.3a^2 a^3 #revise

  +5%, +5%, +5%
  15.75/125
  15.7625 #revise
  
  Similarly,
  +12%, +12%, +12%
  36/432/1728
  40.4928 ]

(a) 42.5%
(b) 45.49%
(c) 40.49% ✔
(d) 41.49%


6. If the base radius and the height of a right circular cone are increased by 10%, then the percentage increase in the volume is:
  [Hint: same as above
  30.300/1000
  33.1000 

  Note: It is useful in CI also ]

(a) 33.1% ✔
(b) 20.2%
(c) 22.1%
(d) 30.2%

IMG:succ-table.png #revise

7. The total percentage change in the volume of a cuboid if its length and breadth are decreased by 15% and 25%, respectively, while its height is increased by 60% is:
  [IMG:AR-lec2-q7.png #revise ]

(a) 5% decrease
(b) 2% decrease
(c) 5% increase
(d) 2% increase ✔


8. A number is first decreased by 10%, then increased by 30% and then further it is decreased by 20%. What is the net decrease percentage in the number?
  [IMG:AR-lec2-q8.png #revise ]

(a) 4 1/5 %
(b) 6 2/5 % ✔
(c) 5 3/5 %
(d) 3 4/5 %


9. A number is first increased by 12% and then increased by 23%. The number, so obtained, is now decreased by 34%. What is the net increase or decrease percent in the original number (nearest to an integer)?
  [Hint: calculative data,
  Do not use ratio method

  Use successive method
  Note: calculative question ]

(a) 10% increase
(b) 9% decrease ✔
(c) 10% decrease
(d) 9% increase


10. Ramnarayan's salary was reduced by 3 1/8 %, and then, the reduced salary was increased by 7 2/5 %. By what percentage (rounded off to two decimal places) is his new salary more/less as compared to his original salary?
  [IMG:AR-lec2-q10.png #revise ]

(a) 3.03% less
(b) 4.04% more ✔
(c) 4.04% less
(d) 3.03% more


11. The length and breadth of a rectangle are in the ratio 5:3. If the length is increased by 44% and Breadth is increased by 60%, What would be the percentage increase in its perimeter?
  [IMG:AR-lec2-q11.png #revise ]

(a) 45%
(b) 46%
(c) 49%
(d) 50% ✔

*Series Method*

*12.* Two years ago, the population of a town was 9487500. Due to migration to big cities, it decreases every year at the rate of 8%. The present population of the town is:
  [Hint: user *Digital Sum* in lengthy calculation, 
  quickly find D.S. of options first ]

(a) 9060110
(b) 7060320
(c) 8070120
(d) 8030220 ✔


*13.* Amit gets 6% increase in his sale amount in the first year and 20% in the second year, with that his present sale is Rs.254400, what was his sale (in Rs.) two years ago?
  [Hint:
  x x 106/100 x 120/100 = 254400 ]

(a) 200000 ✔
(b) 180000
(c) 212000
(d) 240000


14. In the first year the population of a town decreased by 5% due to the Corona virus first wave. In the next year it decreased again by 5% due to the second wave and in the third year it increased by 5%. At the end of the third year the population was 9,47,625. What was the population at the beginning of the first year?
  [Hint: calculative]

(a) 7,00,000
(b) 10,00,000 ✔
(c) 8,97,993
(d) 9,92,519


15. A person spends 25% of his income on goods of daily uses. Furthermore, he spends 18% *of the rest* on house rent and 16% of the rest on travel. After that, only ₹861 is left with him. What is his salary?
  [IMG:AR-lec2-q15.png #revise ]

(a) ₹1852 1/3
(b) ₹1666 2/3 ✔
(c) ₹1563 1/3
(d) ₹1426 2/3


16. The strength of a school increases and decreases every alternate year by 20%. It started with an increase in the year 2015 and the initial strength was 3000. Find the strength of the school in the year 2017 and also the percentage of increase in strength, respectively.
  [Hint: find succ %
  IMG:AR-lec2-q16.png ]

(a) 4556, 17.2%
(b) 3556, 16.2%
(c) 3456, 15.2% ✔
(d) 4456, 14.2%


17. A person, while trading the shares of a particular company, observes that its price has gone down by 10% from the previous day. In anticipation of increment on the next day, he holds it for the next day. But the share price further falls down by another 8% of the previous day. Then he sells his shares and gets Rs.12,420. How much could he have saved had he sold it the previous day?
  [IMG:AR-lec2-q17.png ]

(a) ₹1,080 ✔
(b) ₹1,220
(c) ₹1,260
(d) ₹1,140


---DPQ---

1. The salary of an employee is increased by 10% and then the increased salary is reduced by 10%. The percentage loss in the salary of the employee is:

(a) 1% ✔
(b) 3%
(c) 2%
(d) 4%


2. In a company, all employees are getting equal wages. If the number of employees is increased by 20% and their wages per head are decreased by 18%, what is the percentage decrease in total wages?

(a) 2.4%
(b) 1%
(c) 1.6% ✔
(d) 1.4%


3. The price of a scooter increases successively by 10%, 5% and 15%. What is the total percentage increase in price of scooter?

(a) 32 33/40 % ✔
(b) 32 34/40 %
(c) 32 30/40 %
(d) 32 36/40 %


4. Instead of increasing a number successively by 20 percent and 30 percent, it is decreased by 22 percent. Resultant value is what percentage of the required correct value?

(a) 55%
(b) 60%
(c) 48%
(d) 50% ✔


5. The price of an electronic machine decreased by 5%, 10% and 15% during the first three years. What will be the price of the machine after three years if the value at the beginning was Rs.8,000?

(a) Rs.5000
(b) Rs.6721
(c) Rs.7000
(d) Rs.5814 ✔


6. Two successive increments of 30% each is by what percentage more than two successive decrements of 30% each? (Correct to two decimal places)

(a) 32.54%
(b) 28.15%
(c) 25.25%
(d) 35.29% ✔


7. If the radius of a sphere is increased by 20%, then find the percentage increase in its volume.

(a) 70.6%
(b) 75.5%
(c) 72.8% ✔
(d) 68.5%


8. During the first year the population of a village increased by 5% and during the second year it diminished by 5%. At the end of the second year its population was 47,880. What was the population at the beginning of the first year?

(a) 48000 ✔
(b) 43500
(c) 53000
(d) 45000


9. If due to 12% decrease in the price of sugar, Akshat can buy 7 kg more sugar for ₹ 1,200, then find the actual price (in ₹) of sugar. (Rounded off to 2 decimal places)

(a) 23.38 ✔
(b) 25.79
(c) 26.35
(d) 28.25


10. A woman spends 2/3 of her income. If her income increase by 18% and the expenditure increase by 24%, then the percentage increase in her saving will be:

(a) 6% ✔
(b) 3%
(c) 5%
(d) 4%

TAG:3-percentage
*3-Percentage*

*1.* If the price of rice is reduced by 24%, it allows Alok to buy 10 kg more rice for ₹2,500. The reduced rate of rice per kg is:
  #revisit #revise
  [Hint:
  IMG:AR-per-l3-q1.png ]

(a) ₹25 
(b) ₹50
(c) ₹60 ✔
(d) ₹75


2. A reduction of 15% in the price of washing powder enables a purchaser to obtain 5 kg more for ₹1,275. The original price of the washing powder per kg is:
  [Hint:
  IMG:AR-per-l3-q2.png 
  #revise ]

(a) ₹40
(b) ₹35
(c) ₹45 ✔
(d) ₹50


3. When the price of a commodity increased by 23%, a family reduced its consumption such that the expenditure was only 5% more. By what percentage has the family reduced the consumption (correct to one decimal place)?
  [Hint:
  IMG:AR-per-l3-q3.png
  shortcut: IMG:AR-per-l3-q3-shortcut.png
  #revise ]

(a) 14.20%
(b) 15.8%
(c) 14.6% ✔
(d) 15.2%


4. The price of diesel is increased by 26%. A person wants to increase his expenditure by 15% only. By what percentage should he decrease his consumption (correct to one decimal place)?
  [Hint: 100 wala method
  IMG:AR-per-l3-q4.png
  #revise]

(a) 7.2%
(b) 6.5%
(c) 8.7% ✔
(d) 9.5%

[Income-Expenditure-Saving]

5. The ratio of Richa's expenditure and savings is 2 : 1. If her income and expenditure increase by 20% and 15% respectively, find the percentage increase in her savings.
  [Hint:
  IMG:AR-per-l3-q5.png
  #revise ]

(a) 20%
(b) 35%
(c) 25%
(d) 30% ✔


6. A person saves 10% of his monthly income. If his monthly income increases by 30%, he saves 20% more than the previous savings. The percentage increase in his expenditure (up to two decimal places) is: 
  [Hint: jitna nazar ques pe utna hi nazar options pe
  IMG:AR-per-l3-q6.png #revise ]

(a) 37.33%
(b) 31.11% ✔
(c) 40.44%
(d) 24.89% 


7. Radha saves x% of her income. If her income increases by 28% and the expenditure increases by 20%, then her savings increase by 40%. What is the value of x?
  [Hint: Allegation method
  IMG:AR-per-l3-q7.png
  #revise #revisit]

(a) 35
(b) 40 ✔
(c) 50
(d) 25

[Passing/Failure in an Exam]

*8.* John got 20% marks in an examination and failed by 10 marks. In the same examination, Jack got 35% marks which were 20 more than the minimum passing marks. Find the percentage of minimum marks required to pass.
  [Hint:
  15% -> 30
  1% -> 2
  total marks -> 200
  #revise ]

(a) 30%
(b) 35%
(c) 25% ✔
(d) 20%


9. In an examination a student who got 20% marks failed by 30 marks. Another student who got 32% marks got 42 marks more than the required marks to pass. Find the maximum number of marks.
  [Hint:
  12% -> 72
  1% -> 6
  Total -> 600 ]

(a) 600 ✔
(b) 700
(c) 500
(d) 400

[*Election*]

10. In an election between two candidates, one candidate got 38% of the votes and yet lost by 7200 votes. If all votes were valid, the total votes cast were:
  [Hint:
  38%
  62%

  24% = 7200
  1% = 300
  total = 30,000
  #revise ]

(a) 13,800
(b) 13,000
(c) 16,200
(d) 30,000 ✔


*11.* In an election between two candidates, 75% of eligible voters voted and 6% of the votes cast were invalid. A candidate got 15,228 votes which were 90% of valid votes. Find total eligible voters.
  [Hint:
  IMG:AR-per-l3-q11.png
  #revise ]
(a) 24,850
(b) 27,000
(c) 25,600
(d) 24,000 ✔


12. Two candidates contested an election. 80% voters cast their votes and 5% were invalid. The winner got 70% of valid votes and won by 36,480 votes. Find total voters.
  [Hint:
  IMG:AR-per-l3-q12.png
  #revise #revisit ]

(a) 1,15,000
(b) 1,20,000 ✔
(c) 1,25,000
(d) 1,18,000


13. In an election between two candidates, 3% did not vote and 5% votes were invalid. The winner got 54% of valid votes and won by 11,058 votes. Find the number of voters who did not vote.
  [Hint: similar to above ques.
  into 3% at last
  #revisit ]

(a) 5050
(b) 3750
(c) 4500 ✔
(d) 4125

*[9].* If the selling price of an almirah is doubled, then the profit is tripled. Find the initial profit percentage.
  [Hint: 
  CP = 100  
  SP = x

  Profit₁ = x − 100  
  Profit₂ = 2x − 100
  
  2x − 100 = 3(x − 100)
  2x − 100 = 3x − 300  
  200 = x

  Profit = 200 − 100 = 100  
  Profit % = 100%
  #revisit]

(a) 50%
(b) 10%
(c) 100% ✔
(d) 25%

*17.* By selling two articles for ₹800, a person gains the cost price of three articles. The profit percent is:
  [Hint:
  Let
  CP of 2 articles = ₹20  
  CP of 3 articles = ₹30  

  Profit = ₹30
  SP = CP + Profit
  SP = 20 + 30 = ₹50
  Profit = 30  
  CP = 20  
  Profit % = (30 / 20) × 100
  = 3/2 × 100
  = 150% 
  #revisit ]

(a) 125%
(b) 140%
(c) 120%
(d) 150% ✔

(a) 1/2
(b) 1
(c) 2 ✔
(d) 1/4


3. Simplify:
{[(x – 5)(x – 1)] – [(9x – 5)(9x – 1)]} ÷ 16x

(a) 2x(5x – 3)
(b) –(5x – 3) ✔
(c) x(5x – 3)
(d) –6x(5x – 3)


4. If p + q + r = 0, simplify:
(p² + q² + r²) / (p² – qr + q² – pr + r² – pq)

(a) 0
(b) 2 ✔
(c) 1
(d) –1


5. Simplify:
(x³ + y³ + z³ – 3xyz) / [(x – y)² + (y – z)² + (z – x)²]

(a) (x + y + z)/3
(b) (x + y + z)
(c) (x + y + z)/4
(d) (x + y + z)/2 ✔

6. If (a + b + c) = 14 and (a³ + b³ + c³ – 3abc) = 98,
find the value of (ab + bc + ca).

(a) 60
(b) 64
(c) 65
(d) 63 ✔


7. If (a + b + c) = 12 and (a² + b² + c²) = 50,
find the value of (a³ + b³ + c³ – 3abc).

(a) 36 ✔
(b) 24
(c) 42
(d) 48

find the value of a² + b² + c² – ab – bc – ca.

(b) 4
(c) 3 ✔
(d) 1


9. If (a³ + b³ + c³ – 3abc) = 405 and

find the value of (a + b + c).

(a) 15 ✔
(b) 45
(c) 9
(d) 27


10. If (x + 6)³ + (2x + 3)³ + (3x + 5)³ = (3x + 18)(2x + 3)(3x + 5),
find the value of x.

(a) 7/3
(b) –5/3
(c) 5/3
(d) –7/3 ✔


11. If (a + b + c) = 19 and (a² + b² + c²) = 155,

(a) 104 ✔
(b) 108
(c) 100
(d) 98


12. If a = 101, b = 102 and c = 103,
find the value of a² + b² + c² – ab – bc – ca.

(a) 2b/(a² + b²)
(b) a/(a² + b²) ✔
(c) b/(a² + b²)

14. Simplify:
(25a² – 10ab – 48b²)/(5a + 6b) × (5a + 8b)

(a) 25a² – 64b² ✔
(b) (5a – 8b)²

30. In a party hall, there are people in blue and red dresses. The ratio of number of men in blue to the number of women in red is 3 : 7. (b) 40 : 43
(c) 62 : 57
(d) 52 : 59 ✔

(c) 44
(d) 38

(c) 5
(d) 2

Proportion
TYPE - 1

1. The first proportional of three numbers 6, 12 and 24 is :

(a) 3 ✔
(b) 4
(c) 7
(d) 6


2. The second proportional of three numbers 28, 4 and 5 is :

(a) 39
(b) 48
(c) 35 ✔
(d) 40


3. Find the third proportional of 9, 7, ?, 14.

(a) 18 ✔
(b) 16
(c) 24
(d) 21


4. Find the fourth proportional to 4, 9 and 16.

(a) 18
(b) 27
(c) 36 ✔
(d) 16


5. Find the ratio between the fourth proportional of 42, 56, 63 and the fourth proportional of 189, 273, and 153.

(a) 33 : 84
(b) 217 : 42
(c) 33 : 221
(d) 84 : 221 ✔


TYPE - 2

6. The mean proportional of 2 & 32 is:

(a) 16
(b) 8 ✔
(c) 12
(d) 6

(a) √238 + 36√2 ✔
(b) √238 + 120√2
(c) √238 + 84√2
(d) √238 + 110√2


8. Find the third proportion to 36 & 48.

(a) 54
(b) 36
(c) 48
(d) 64 ✔

(a) 3, 38
(b) 3, 28
(c) 24, 6 ✔
(d) 24, 16


10. If 28.9 : x :: x : 36.1, and x > 0, then find the value of x.

(a) 38.3
(b) 32.3 ✔
(c) 30.4
(d) 35


11. If p is the third proportional to 8, 20 and q is the fourth proportional to 3, 5, 24 , then find the value of (2p + q).

(a) 140 ✔
(b) 126
(c) 90
(d) 104


TYPE - 3

12. Which number should be added to 3, 11, 4 and 14 to make them in proportion?

(a) 2
(b) 1 ✔
(c) 3
(d) 4


13. When x is added to each of 22, 26, 19 and 21, then the numbers so obtained, in this order, are in proportion. Then, if 2x : y :: y : (4x – 8), and y > 0, what is the value of y?

(a) 48 ✔
(b) 37
(c) 46
(d) 54


14. If x is subtracted from each of 24, 40, 33 and 57, the numbers, so obtained are in proportion. The ratio of (5x + 12) to (4x + 15) is

(a) 4 : 3
(b) 14 : 13 ✔
(c) 7 : 4
(d) 7 : 5

(a) 30
(b) 35 ✔
(c) 20
(d) 42



TYPE - 4

16. A varies directly as (B + 18) and A = 108 when B = 36. Find the value of A when B = 68.

(a) 75
(b) 86
(c) 127
(d) 172 ✔

(a) 1/2 ✔
(b) 1
(c) 69
(d) 1/4


18. X is directly proportional to A² and A is inversely proportional to Y. If X is 97 when Y is 6, find X when Y is 2.

(a) 873 ✔
(b) 871
(c) 872
(d) 875


19. A function of two variable varies directly with x and inversely with y. Determine function when x = 5 and y = 3. Given that, for x = 0 and y = 1, f = 15 and for x = 1 and y = 15, f = 2.

(a) 10 ✔
(b) 2
(c) 5
(d) 15

(a) 3 : 2
(b) 2 : 3
(c) 3 : 4
(d) 4 : 3 ✔

*34-Mixture-and-allegation*

1. In a mixture of 25 litres, the ratio of acid to water is 4 : 1. Another 3 litres of water is added to the mixture. The ratio of acid to water in the new mixture is

(a) 5 : 2 ✔
(b) 2 : 5
(c) 3 : 5
(d) 5 : 3

(a) 8 ✔
(b) 6
(c) 5
(d) 4

(a) 10%
(b) 60%
(c) 30%
(d) 25% ✔

(a) 18 L
(b) 28 L
(c) 30 L
(d) 42 L ✔

(a) 25 litres
(b) 40 litres
(c) 35 litres
(d) 30 litres ✔

(b) 1.5
(c) 0.5
(d) 1 ✔

(b) 1
(c) 3
(d) 4

---Type 3---

1. The temperatures recorded over five consecutive days in a town were: 28°C, 30°C, 32°C, 31°C and 29°C. What was the average temperature during these five days?

(d) 83 ✔

(d) 83

(c) 64
(d) 57

(c) 163.4
(d) 161.4

(d) ₹7,355

*36-Time-and-Work*
1. Akhil can complete a work in 24 days. Shyam can complete the same work in 12 days. If both of them work together, in how many days can they complete the same work?
  [Hint:
  LCM of 12 & 24 = 24
  In 1 day: A -> 1 unit; S -> 2 unit
  Total work in 1 day = 3 unit
  24 / 3 = 8
  ]

(a) 6 days
(b) 8 days ✔
(c) 10 days
(d) 12 days


2. A can complete 1/3 of a work in 7 days and B can complete 2/7 of the same work in 10 days. In how many days can both A and B together complete the work?

(a) 12 3/8
(b) 11 7/8
(c) 13 1/8 ✔
(d) 15 1/7


*3.* Sumit and Rajiv, working together, can do a work in 20 hours whereas Sumit alone can do the same work in 25 hours. In how many hours can Rajiv alone do the work?

(a) 70
(b) 90
(c) 80 
(d) 100 ✔


4. A and B complete a work in 18 days. If A alone can do it in 24 days, then B alone can do one-fourth of the same work in ______ days.
  [Hint:
  LCM = 72  
  (A+B) = 4  
  A = 3  

  B = (A+B) - A
  4 - 3
  1
  B = 1 → Time = 72
  72 / 4 = 18]

(a) 18 ✔
(b) 72
(c) 36
(d) 54


*5.* A can do 20% of a work in 7 days and B can do 25% of the work in 7 days if they worked alone. How much of the work (in percentage) can they complete in 7 days if they worked together?

(a) 38%
(b) 52%
(c) 56%
(d) 45% ✔

(b) 5
(c) 1 ✔
(d) 4


*7.* A can do 20% of a work in 4 days and B can do 33 1/3% of the same work in 10 days. They worked together for 9 days and then C finished the remaining work in 6 days. In how many days will B and C together complete 75% of the same work?

(a) 12 days
(b) 9 days
(c) 11 days
(d) 10 days ✔


8. A can do 1/3 of a work in 15 days, B can do 3/4 of the same work in 18 days and C can do the same work in 36 days. B and C work together for 8 days. In how many days will A alone complete the remaining work?
  [Hint: long calculation, super easy question]

(a) 24 days
(b) 18 days
(c) 20 days ✔
(d) 16 days


*9.* A and B can do a piece of work in 10 days. B and C can do the same work in 12 days. C and A can do the same work in 15 days. If all the three work together, find the number of days required to complete the work.

(b) 10
(c) 8
(d) 12 ✔

(b) 17/27

(d) 7/27 ✔

*38-Pipe-and-cistern*

1. Pipe L can fill a pool in 30 hours and pipe M in 45 hours. If both the pipes are opened in an empty pool, how much time will they take to fill it?

(b) 17 hrs.
(c) 18 hrs. ✔

2. A tank can be filled by pipe A in 4 hours and pipe B in 6 hours. At 8:00 a.m., pipe A was opened. At what time will the tank be filled if pipe B is opened at 9:00 a.m.?

(a) 10:16 a.m.
(b) 10:22 a.m.
(c) 10:48 a.m. ✔
(d) 10:18 a.m.


3. Pipes A, B and C can fill a tank in 20, 30 and 60 hours, respectively. Pipes A, B and C are opened at 7 a.m., 8 a.m., & 9 a.m., respectively, on the same day. When will the tank be filled?

(a) 4:40 p.m.
(b) 5:40 p.m. ✔
(c) 6:20 p.m.
(d) 7:20 p.m.


4. Two pipes P1 and P2 together can fill a cistern in 8 hours. Had they been opened separately, then P2 would have taken 12 hours more than P1 to fill the cistern. How much time will be taken by P1 alone to fill the cistern?

(a) 12 hours ✔
(b) 10 hours
(c) 8 hours
(d) 11 hours


5. A tap can fill a cistern in 10 minutes and another tap can empty it in 12 minutes. If both the taps are open, the time (in hours) taken to fill the tank will be:

(a) 1.5 hours
(b) 2.5 hours
(c) 2 hours
(d) 1 hour ✔


6. Pipes P and Q can completely fill a water tank in 10 hours and 15 hours, respectively. A pipe R can empty a tank filled completely with water in 12 hours. Initially, the tank is empty and only pipes P and Q are opened at 6 a.m. and pipe R is also opened at 9 a.m. By what time will the tank be completely filled?

(a) 1 p.m
(b) 2 p.m
(c) 11 p.m
(d) 3 p.m ✔


7. An inlet pipe can fill an empty tank in 140 hours while an outlet pipe drains a completely filled tank in 63 hours. If 8 inlet pipes and y outlet pipes are opened simultaneously, when the tank is empty, then the tank gets completely filled in 105 hours. Find the value of y.

(a) 1
(b) 4
(c) 3 ✔
(d) 2


8. Inlet Pipes A and B can together fill an empty tank in 1.5 hours. Outlet Pipe C, when opened alone, can empty the completely filled tank, in 4.5 hours. When only Pipes A and C are opened together, the empty tank is filled in 6 hours. Find the time taken by Pipe B, when opened alone, to fill the empty tank.

(a) 3 hours 30 min.
(b) 3 hours 36 min. ✔
(c) 3 hours 32 min.
(d) 3 hours 40 min.


9. Pipe Q can fill the tank in 60 hours while pipe R may fill in 45 hours. Q and R pipes are opened together for 6 hours after which pipe W is also opened to empty the tank. All three pipes are opened simultaneously for 24 hours to reach the half level mark. How much time (in hours) will pipe W alone take to empty the entire tank?

(a) 48
(b) 42
(c) 36 ✔
(d) 30


10. Pipe P can fill 4/9 of a tank in 28 hours, and pipe Q can fill 3/5 of the same tank in 27 hours. Both pipes P and Q are opened for 3 hours, then both are closed. After that, only pipe R is opened, which empties the tank in 8 hours. If pipes P, Q, and R are opened together, how long will it take to fill the empty tank?

(a) 51 hours
(b) 57 hours
(c) 40 hours
(d) 42 hours ✔


11. There are two water taps in a tank which can fill the empty tank in 12 hours and 18 hours respectively. It is seen that there is a leakage point at the bottom of the tank which can empty the completely filled tank in 36 hours. If both the water taps are opened at the same time to fill the empty tank and the leakage point was repaired after 1 hour, then in how much time the empty tank will be completely filled?

(a) 7 hours 12 min.
(b) 8 hours 24 min.
(c) 7 hours
(d) 7 hours 24 min. ✔


12. Two pipes A and B can fill a cistern in 12 1/2 hours and 25 hours, respectively. The pipes were opened simultaneously, and it was found that, due to leakage in the bottom, it took one hour 40 minutes more to fill the cistern. If the cistern is full, in how much time (in hours) will the leak alone empty 70% of the cistern?

(a) 35 ✔
(b) 40
(c) 30
(d) 50


13. Two pipes A and B can fill a tank in 20 and 30 hours, respectively. Both pipes are opened to fill the tank, but when the tank is one-third full, a leak develops through which one-fourth of the water supplied by both pipes goes out. Find the total time (in hours) taken to fill the tank.

(a) 14 2/3 ✔
(b) 14
(c) 11 2/5
(d) 12 1/3


14. An inlet pipe can fill an empty tank in 4 1/2 hours while an outlet pipe drains a completely filled tank in 7 1/5 hours. In how many hours will the tank be completely filled?

(a) 24
(b) 20 1/3
(c) 20 3/4 ✔
(d) 22 1/2


15. A tank when full can be emptied by an outlet pipe A in 5.6 hours, while an inlet pipe B can fill the same empty tank in 7 hours. If pipes A and B are turned on alternately for 1 hour each starting with pipe A when the tank is full, how long will it take to empty the tank?

(a) 48 hours
(b) 47 hours ✔
(c) 56 hours
(d) 55 hours


16. A tank is filled through three pipes x, y, and z. Pipe x and y alone can fill the tank in 30 hours and 45 hours, respectively. In the first hour, pipes x and z fill the tank, and in the second hour, pipes y and z fill the tank, and this process continues in this way, filling 70% of the tank in 15 hours. If pipe z, when opened along with pipes x and y, provides 75% of the original supply, how much time will pipe z take to fill the tank by itself?

(a) 40.5 hours ✔
(b) 56.25 hours
(c) 54 hours
(d) 45 hours


17. Two pipes can fill a tank separately in 36 minutes and 45 minutes respectively. A drain pipe installed in the tank can remove 40 liters of water per minute. If all three pipes are opened together, the tank is filled in one hour. Find the capacity/holding (in litres) of the tank.

(a) 600
(b) 400
(c) 300
(d) 1200 ✔


18. Pipes A and B can fill an empty cistern in 72 minutes and 76 minutes, respectively. Both Pipe A and B are opened together. After how much time should Pipe B be turned off so that the empty cistern is completely filled in a total of 54 minutes?

(a) 13 min.
(b) 17 min.
(c) 19 min. ✔
(d) 23 min.


19. Pipes A and B can fill a tank in 18 hours and 27 hours, respectively, whereas pipe C can empty the full tank in 54 hours. All three pipes are opened together, but pipe C is closed after 12 hours. (a) 24 ✔
(b) 36
(c) 30
(d) 15


20. Pipes M, N and S can fill a tank in 25, 50 and 100 minutes, respectively. Initially, pipes N and S are kept open for 10 minutes, and then pipe N is shut while pipe M is opened. (a) 30
(b) 33
(c) 42
(d) 27 ✔


21. A cistern can be filled by two pipes in 8 minutes and 10 minutes, separately. Both the pipes are opened together for a certain time, but due to an obstruction, only 5/8 of the full quantity of water flowed through the former pipe and 3/5 through the latter pipe. (a) 3 1/16 minutes
(b) 2 6/17 minutes ✔
(c) 9 6/7 minutes
(d) 2 30/37 minutes


22. Pipe A takes 4/5 of the time required by pipe B to fill an empty tank individually. When an outlet pipe C is also opened simultaneously with pipes A and B, it takes 4/5 more time to fill the empty tank than it takes when only pipe A and pipe B are opened together. (a) 50 hours ✔
(b) 45 hours
(c) 65 hours
(d) 75 hours


23. The tank is filled by three pipes with different uniform flow rates. While the first two pipes are operating simultaneously, they fill the tank in the same duration that the third pipe takes to fill it alone. (b) 12

(d) 15 ✔


24. There are 30 pipes connected to a tank, some of which are filling pipes, and the remaining are draining pipes. (a) 6
(b) 8 ✔
(c) 10
(d) 12


25. Pipes A and B are connected to a tank. A is the filling pipe and B can be used to fill or dispense at the same rate. When B is used for filling, it takes 't' time to fill the tank. (a) 5 : 1
(b) 1 : 3

TAG:42-time-and-distance
*42-time-and-distance*

1. Which of the following is NOT a correct statement?

(a) The speed of 20 m/s is less than the speed of 85 km/h.
(b) Time may be calculated by dividing the distance by the speed.
(c) Covering the same distance in lesser time implies a higher speed.
(d) The speed of 99 km/h is less than the speed of 24 m/s. ✔


*2.* To reach at a destination, D takes 45 minutes if he drives at a speed of 60 km/h. Due to some urgency, he is to reach the destination in 30 minutes. What should be his speed in km/h?
  [Hint: 
  T -> 45 : 30
  T -> 3 : 2
  S -> 2 : 3
  2 = 60 km/h; 3 = 90 km/hr]

(a) 80
(b) 75
(c) 90 ✔
(d) 60

*3.* Walking at 5/7 of his normal speed, Manish is 20 minutes late in reaching his office. The usual time taken by him to cover the distance between his home and his office is:
  [Hint:
  5/7 ; Here 7 -> old speed; 5 -> new speed;
  S -> 7 : 5
  T -> 5 : 7
  Diff = 2

  Method 2:
  5/7 => 20 min
  7 - 5 = 2
  50 x 2 / 2
  50 km/hr]

(a) 56 minutes
(b) 42 minutes
(c) 50 minutes ✔
(d) 49 minutes


*[4.]* A train can travel 75% faster than a car. Both start from point A at the same time and reach point B, 70 km from A, at the same time. However, the train loses about 18 minutes in stopping at stations on the way. What is the speed of the car?
  [Hint:  ]

(a) 90 km/h
(b) 100 km/h ✔
(c) 80 km/h
(d) 110 km/h


*[5.]* Devender leaves his home everyday at 8 : 25 am and reaches office at 9:55 am. One day, he left his home at 8 : 25 am but travelled 3/10 of the total distance at 6/7 of the usual speed and the rest of the distance at 7/6 of the usual speed. At what time did Devender reach office on that day?

(a) 9 : 50 : 30 (am) ✔
(b) 9 : 50 : 40 (am)
(c) 9 : 50 : 50 (am)
(d) 9 : 50 : 20 (am)


6. To cover a distance of 416 km, a train A takes 2/3 hours more than train B. If the speed of A is doubled, It would take 1/3 hours less than B. What is the speed (in km/h) of train A?

(a) 56
(b) 54
(c) 52 ✔
(d) 65


7. Jia takes 50 minutes less than Pia to cover 50 km. However, if Jia reduces her speed to half of her previous speed, then she takes 1 2/3 hrs more than Pia to cover the same distance. What is the speed of Pia (in km/hr)?

(a) 20
(b) 10
(c) 15 ✔
(d) 12

---Type III---

*8.* A person travels from one place to another at 60 km/hr and returns at 75 km/hr. If the total time taken is 6 hours, then find the total distance travelled.
  [Hint:
  *Average Speed for Equal Distance*
  Avg Speed = 2ab/a+b
  2 x 60 x 75 / 135
  *Total Distance*
  Total Distance = (2ab / (a + b)) × Total Time
  9000 / 135 x 6
  ]

(a) 300 km
(b) 240 km
(c) 250 km
(d) 400 km ✔


*9.* A student goes to school at a speed of 5 1/2 km/h and returns at a speed of 4 km/h. If he takes 4 3/4 hours for the entire journey, then the total distance covered by the student (in km) is:
  [Hint:
  5 1/2 = 11/2
  4 3/4 = 19/4
  a = 11/2; b = 4; time = 19/4

  Total Distance = (2ab / (a + b)) × Total Time
  ( 2 x 11/2 x 4 x 19/4 ) / (a + b)
  209/(19/2)
  22]

(a) 11
(b) 22 ✔
(c) 16
(d) 24


*10.* A person cycles from the hostel to the college at a speed of 20 km/h and reaches 13.5 minutes late. If he cycles at a speed of 24 km/h and reaches 13.5 minutes early, find the distance (in km) between the hostel and the college.
  [Hint:
  13.5 + 13.5 = 27 min
  Distance = (20 × 24 × 27) / (60 × 4) 
  54
  27 is in minutes, but speed is in km/hour, so 60 at bottom
  ]

(a) 50
(b) 52
(c) 54 ✔
(d) 48


*[11.]* A boy when goes to his school by 12 km/hr speed, reaches 20 mins late and when he covers the distance by 16 km/hr, reaches 5 mins late. Find speed by which he may reach on time and also find distance of his school.
  [Hint:
  15 min
  (12 x 16 x 15) / (60 x 4)
  12 km (distance)

  Speed = d/t
  12 / (40/60)
  ]

(a) 16 km/hr, 12 km
(b) 18 km/hr, 12 km ✔
(c) 20 km/hr, 10 km
(d) 15 km/hr, 10 km


12. Annu covers certain distance with her own speed, but when she reduces her speed by 10 km/hr, her time duration for the journey increases by 40 hr, but when she increases her original speed by 15 km/hr time taken by her is 10 hours less than the original time. Find the distance covered by her.
  [Hint:
  Speed ↓10 → time +40
  Speed ↑15 → time −10

  Total time swing
  40 + 10 = 50 hours

  10 × 15 × 50 / 25 = 300

  How 25 came?
  Speeds are:
  Lower speed = original − 10  
  Higher speed = original + 15

  Difference between two speeds
  (Original + 15) − (Original − 10)

  Originals cancels
  = 15 + 10 = 25

  ]

(a) 300 km ✔
(b) 280 km
(c) 320 km
(d) 350 km


13. A person had to cover a certain distance with bike in 48 min but after travelling for 36 min his speed is reduced by 10 km/h and he takes 3 min more than usual to cover the remaining distance, then find actual speed of bike.
  [Hint: 
  12 → 15 ⇒ 4:5  
  Difference = 1 part = 10  
  So speed = 5 × 10 = 50]

(a) 50 km/h ✔
(b) 48 km/h
(c) 54 km/h
(d) 51 km/h


14. Time taken by car A to cover 32 km is 8 min less than that taken by car B to cover the same distance. If speed of car B is increased by 36 km/h, then it takes 4 min less than car A to cover the same distance, then find the actual speed of car B.

(a) 66 km/h
(b) 72 km/h
(c) 60 km/h ✔
(d) 63 km/h


15. Time taken by Piyush to finish a race of 7.5 km is 1 min more than that taken by Ayush to finish that race. If Piyush increases his speed by one - third, then he can finish the race 1.5 min prior to Ayush, then find the time taken Piyush to finish the race with actual speed.

(a) 7.5 min
(b) 12.5 min
(c) 8 min
(d) 10 min ✔


16. A journey of 600 km takes 11 hours if 120 km is covered by train and the rest by car. If the same journey is covered 200 km by train and the rest by car, it takes 40 minutes more. What is the ratio of the speed of the car to the speed of the train?

(a) 3 : 2 ✔
(b) 2 : 3
(c) 3 : 4
(d) 4 : 3


17. A person ride one-third of a journey at 60 km/hr, one-third at 50 km/hr and the rest at 40 km/hr. Had the person ridden half of the journey at 60 km/hr and the rest at 40 km/hr, he would have taken 4 minutes longer to complete the journey. What distance did the person ride?

(a) 180 km
(b) 210 km
(c) 240 km ✔
(d) 300 km


18. Rama walks to her office 5 km away from home. In the morning, she covers the distance in 1 hour whereas, while returning home in the evening, she takes 15 more minutes to cover the same distance. Find her average speed (in km/h) during the two-way journey.

(b) 4 8/9 ✔
(c) 3 7/8
(d) 4 4/7


19. A person covers 1/4 of his journey at the speed of 25 km/h, 1/2 of the journey at 40km/h and the remaining at the speed of 50 km/h. Find his average speed per hour for the whole journey (in km/h).

(a) 36 4/11 ✔
(b) 34 6/11
(c) 36 6/11
(d) 34 4/11


20. The ratio of the distance between two places A and B to the distance between places B and C is 3 : 5. A man travels from A to B at a speed of x km/h and from B to C at a speed of 50 km/h. If his average speed for the entire journey is 40 km/h, then what is the value of (x - 10) : (x + 1)?

(a) 20 : 31 ✔
(b) 31 : 20
(c) 11 : 10
(d) 10 : 11


21. Yash travels 204 km at 68 km/hr, the next 424 km at 53 km/hr and the next 366 km at 61 km/hr. What is his average speed (in km/hr) for the whole journey? (Corrected to two decimal places)

(b) 57.62
(c) 58.47 ✔
(d) 65.87


22. A man has to cover a distance of 549 km in 8 hours. If he covers 2/3 of this distance in 3/4 of the time, then what should be his speed (in km/hr) to cover the remaining distance in the time left?

*43-Train-boat-stream*

*1.* A train running at 40 1/2 km/h takes 24 second to cross a pole. How much time (in second) will it take to pass a 450 m long bridge?
  [Hint:
  Speed = 81/2 km/h
  81/2 x 5/18 m/s

  9/2 x 5/2
  45/4 m/s

  so, s = 45/4 m/s;
  t = 24
  s = d/t
  d = s x t
  45/4 x 24
  270

  s = d / t
  t = d / s
  (450 + 270) / (45/4)

  720 / (45/4)
  64 ]

(a) 56
(b) 52
(c) 60
(d) 64 ✔


*2.* Two trains of lengths 250 metres and 200 metres run on parallel tracks. When running in the same direction, the faster train crosses the slower one in 37.5 seconds. When running in opposite directions at speeds the same as their earlier speeds, they pass each other completely in 7.5 seconds. Then the ratio of the speeds of the faster train to the slower train is:

(a) 3 : 2 ✔
(b) 5 : 4
(c) 4 : 3
(d) 6 : 5


3. Train A running at 81 km/h takes 72 sec to overtake train B, when both the trains are running in the same direction, but it takes 36 sec to cross each other if the trains are running in the opposite direction. If the length of train B is 600 metres, then find the length of train A. (in metres)

(a) 600
(b) 480 ✔
(c) 590
(d) 900


4. A 240m long train X passes a pole in 18 seconds and completely crosses another train Y running at a speed of 72 km/h in the opposite direction in 21 seconds. How much time (in seconds) will train Y take to completely cross a 140m long train Z running at a speed of 42 km/h in the same direction?

(a) 68 sec.
(b) 65 sec.
(c) 72 sec. ✔
(d) 70 sec.

(a) 2
(b) 1
(c) 1 1/4
(d) 1 1/2 ✔

(b) Both I and II
(c) Only II
(d) Only I

Question: How much time (in hours) will a boat take to travel 25 km downstream?
Statement I: The time taken by a boat to travel a certain distance downstream is 7/10 of the time taken to cover the same distance in still water.
Statement II: The boat takes 6 hours to travel 49 km downstream and 14 km upstream.
Statement III: The ratio of the speed of the boat in still water to the speed of the current is 7 : 3.

(a) Only I and II
(b) Only II and III
(c) I and II or II and III ✔
(d) Only I and III

(d) 180 km

(c) 250
(d) 300


10. Two trains of lengths 150 m and 250 m run on parallel lines. When they run in the same direction, they take 20 seconds to cross each other and, when they run in the opposite direction, they take 5 seconds to cross each other. What is the speed of the two trains?

(a) 150 km/h and 105 km/h
(b) 150 km/h and 250 km/h
(c) 180 km/h and 108 km/h ✔
(d) 160 km/h and 106 km/h


11. Train A leaves station X at 8.00 am and travels towards station Y which is 250 km away. Another train B leaves station Y at 10.00 am and goes towards station X. The ratio of speed of train A to that of train B is 8 : 9. The distance between station Y, and the place where train A leaves at 10 AM, is 170 km. At what distance from station Y and at what time both the trains will meet?

(a) 125 km, 2 pm
(b) 160 km, 12 pm
(c) 90 km, 12 pm ✔
(d) 80 km, 2 pm


12. A train A starts from place D at 6:00 am in the morning and reaches place G at 10:00 am in the morning. Train B departs from place G at 8:00 am and reaches place D at 11:30 am. If the distance between places D and G is 200 km, then what is the time when both the trains meet each other?

(a) 8:51 am
(b) 9:01 am
(c) 9:06 am
(d) 8:56 am ✔


13. A train 75 meters long overtook a person who was walking at 6 km/hr in the opposite direction and passed him in 7 1/2 seconds. Subsequently it overtook a second person, walking in the same directions as the 1st person and passed him in 6 3/4 seconds. At what rate was the second person travelling ?

(a) 11 3/4 km/hr
(b) 10 km/hr ✔
(c) 8 km/hr
(d) 4 1/2 km/hr


14. A train crosses 130 metre long platform in 14.5 seconds and 245 metre long platform in 20.25 seconds. What is the speed of the train?

(a) 69 km/hr
(b) 75 km/hr
(c) 66 km/hr
(d) 72 km/hr ✔


15. Train A overtakes train B which is going in opposite direction in 54 seconds which is twice the length of A and running at half the speed of train A. Train A crosses another train C going in opposite direction in 20 seconds whose speed is twice that of train A. If the speed of train A is 60 km/h, then what is the length of train C?

(a) 650 m
(b) 550 m ✔
(c) 250 m
(d) 450 m


16. The ratio of the speeds of a boat while going upstream and going downstream is 2 : 3 and the sum of these two speeds is 15 km/h. What is the speed of the stream ?

(a) 3.5 km/h
(b) 1.5 km/h ✔
(c) 3 km/h
(d) 2.5 km/h


17. The speed of a boat in still water is 25 km/h. It takes 33 1/3 % more time to cover a certain distance in still water than to cover the same distance downstream. How much time in hours will boat take to go 75 km downstream?

(a) 3
(b) 2.25 ✔
(c) 2
(d) 1.5


18. A boat can travel 78 km upstream and back in a total of 32 hours. It can travel 15 km upstream and 52 km downstream in a total of 9 hours. How much distance will the boat cover in 12 hours in still water?

(a) 92 km
(b) 96 km ✔
(c) 104 km
(d) 100 km


19. The ratio of the speed of a motorboat to that of the current of water is 31:6. The motorboat starts from a point and covers a certain distance along the current in 4 h 10 min. Find the time taken by the motorboat to come back to its initial point.

(a) 4 h 10 min
(b) 5 h 10 min
(c) 5 h 50 min
(d) 6 h 10 min ✔


20. The time taken by a boat to cover a distance of x km upstream is double the time taken by the boat to cover the same distance downstream. The sum of the speeds of the boat and the stream is 90 km/h. The speed of the stream is ___ km/h.

(a) 22.5 ✔
(b) 33.5
(c) 27.5
(d) 37.5


21. A motorboat travelling at a certain speed can cover a distance of 24 km upstream and 40 km downstream in 17 hours. At the same speed it can travel 32 km downstream and 12 km upstream in 10 hours. What is the speed of the current?

(a) 5 km/h
(b) 4 km/h
(c) 2 km/h
(d) 3 km/h ✔


22. A motorboat, whose speed in 15 km/h in still water goes 50 km down-stream and comes back in a total of 7 hours 30 minutes. The speed of the stream (in km/h) is?

(a) 9 km/h
(b) 5 km/h ✔
(c) 11 km/h
(d) 7 km/h


23. A man rows to a place 48 km distant and comes back in 14 hours. He finds that he can row 4 km with the stream in the same time as 3 km against the stream. The speed of the stream is:

(a) 1.5 km/h
(b) 3.5 km/h
(c) 1.8 km/h
(d) 1 km/h ✔


24. The speed of a boat in still water is 18 km/h and the speed of the stream is 3 km/h. How much time (in hours) will it take to cover a distance of 105 km in downstream and in coming back?

(a) 12 ✔
(b) 10
(c) 15
(d) 9


25. The speed of a boat in still water is 6 km/h and the speed of the stream is 1.5 km/h. In going from point A to point B and returning to A, the boatman takes 2 hours 40 min. Find the distance between points A and B.

(a) 7.5 km ✔
(b) 7 km
(c) 8 km
(d) 8.5 km


26. Suresh covers a distance of 34 km in the direction of a river in 4 hours 15 minutes by a luxury boat and 19 km in the opposite direction of a river in 3 hours 10 minutes. What is the speed of the flow of river?

(a) 3 km/hr
(b) 2 km/hr
(c) 1 km/hr ✔
(d) 5 km/hr


27. A man can row at the speed of 8.5 km/h in still water. In a river running at the speed of 1.5 km/h, it takes him 51 minutes to row to a place and come back. How far (in km) is this place?

(a) 4.5
(b) 5.5
(c) 7.5
(d) 3.5 ✔


28. A person swims at a speed of 5 km/h in still water in a river whose speed is 1 km/h. It takes 75 minutes to swim from position A to position B. What is the distance between A and B?

(a) 6 km
(b) 5 km
(c) 2.5 km
(d) 3 km ✔


29. A boat takes 7 hours to move 63 km downstream and 30 km upstream. The boat takes 6 hours to move 28 km downstream and 48 km upstream. How much time will it take to move 35km downstream and 27km upstream?

(a) 4 hrs 45 min ✔
(b) 4 hrs 50 min
(c) 5 hrs
(d) 5 hrs 20 min


30. 15 hours is taken by a boat to reach its destination in still water and return to its starting point from there. The same journey requires 16 hours if the river flows. The difference between the speed of boat and the river is 15 km/hr. Find the speed of the flow of river.

(a) 10 km/hrs
(b) 6 km/hrs
(c) 4 km/hrs
(d) 5 km/hrs ✔
